# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repository:** `github.com/sg-evals/transformers--07ae53e6`
- Use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/transformers--07ae53e6$` filter in keyword_search
- Use `github.com/sg-evals/transformers--07ae53e6` as the `repo` parameter for go_to_definition/find_references/read_file


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Fix: SWE-PolyBench__python__maintenance__bugfix__40f09c26

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/transformers--07ae53e6 (mirror of huggingface/transformers)
**Language:** python
**Category:** contextbench_cross_validation

## Description

Issue with Adding New Tokens to ESM2 Model Tokenizer
Hello

I am encountering an issue while working with the ESM2 models (`facebook/esm2_t6_8M_UR50D`). Specifically, when I try to add new tokens to the tokenizer, they are automatically classified as special tokens, even though I am specifying `special_tokens=False`.

Here is the code snippet I am using:

```python
model_checkpoint = "facebook/esm2_t6_8M_UR50D"
model = AutoModelForMaskedLM.from_pretrained(model_checkpoint)
tokenizer = AutoTokenizer.from_pretrained(model_checkpoint)
num_added_toks = tokenizer.add_tokens(['J'], special_tokens=False)
print("We have added", num_added_toks, "tokens")
model.resize_token_embeddings(len(tokenizer))
```

After executing this code, the new token ('J') is added as a special token, which is not the intended behavior. This behavior is different compared to when I use similar code with BERT models, where new tokens are added as expected without being automatically marked as special.

The vocab output is below:
```python
<bound method EsmTokenizer.get_vocab of EsmTokenizer(name_or_path=‘facebook/esm2_t6_8M_UR50D’, vocab_size=33, model_max_length=1024, is_fast=False, padding_side=‘right’, truncation_side=‘right’, special_tokens={‘eos_token’: ‘’, ‘unk_token’: ‘’, ‘pad_token’: ‘’, ‘cls_token’: ‘’, ‘mask_token’: ‘’, ‘additional_special_tokens’: [‘J’]}, clean_up_tokenization_spaces=True), added_tokens_decoder={
0: AddedToken(“”, rstrip=False, lstrip=False, single_word=False, normalized=False, special=True),
1: AddedToken(“”, rstrip=False, lstrip=False, single_word=False, normalized=False, special=True),
2: AddedToken(“”, rstrip=False, lstrip=False, single_word=False, normalized=False, special=True),
3: AddedToken(“”, rstrip=False, lstrip=False, single_word=False, normalized=False, special=True),
32: AddedToken(“”, rstrip=False, lstrip=False, single_word=False, normalized=False, special=True),
33: AddedToken(“J”, rstrip=False, lstrip=False, single_word=False, normalized=False, special=True),
}>
```
My main problem is that I noticed the **length of the tokenizer** does not change after adding the new token and therefore the above code does not extend the embeddings layer as expected.

I'm seeking guidance or a workaround for this issue. Is this a known issue with the ESM2 tokenizer, or am I missing something in my implementation?

Any help or insight into this matter would be greatly appreciated.

Thank you!

9-assistanttext-
Perfect! I found the bug. On line 161-162 of the EsmTokenizer, the `_add_tokens` method is hardcoding `special_tokens=True` regardless of what the user specifies:

```python
def _add_tokens(self, new_tokens: Union[List[str], List[AddedToken]], special_tokens: bool = False) -> int:
    return super()._add_tokens(new_tokens, special_tokens=True)
```

Let me check the test file to understand what the expected behavior should be:

84-assistanttext-
Now I understand the issues. There are three main problems:

1. **Line 162**: The `_add_tokens` method forces `special_tokens=True` regardless of user input
2. **Line 98**: The `get_vocab()` method only returns base tokens, not added tokens
3. **Lines 95-99**: The vocab size and vocabulary don't account for added tokens

Let me fix these issues:

    87→

    89→        return self._token_to_id.get(token, self._token_to_id.get(self.unk_token))
    90→
    91→    def _tokenize(self, text, **kwargs):

    def test_add_tokens_tokenizer(self):
        tokenizers: List[LayoutLMv3Tokenizer] = self.get_tokenizers(do_lower_case=False)
        for tokenizer in tokenizers:
            with self.subTest(f"{tokenizer.__class__.__name__}"):
                vocab_size = tokenizer.vocab_size
                all_size = len(tokenizer)

                self.assertNotEqual(vocab_size, 0)

                # We usually have added tokens from the start in tests because our vocab fixtures are
                # smaller than the original vocabs - let's not assert this
                # self.assertEqual(vocab_size, all_size)

                new_toks = ["aaaaa", "bbbbbb", "cccccccccdddddddd"]
                added_toks = tokenizer.add_tokens(new_toks)
                vocab_size_2 = tokenizer.vocab_size
                all_size_2 = len(tokenizer)

                self.assertNotEqual(vocab_size_2, 0)
                self.assertEqual(vocab_size, vocab_size_2)
                self.assertEqual(added_toks, len(new_toks))
                self.assertEqual(all_size_2, all_size + len(new_toks))

                words = "aaaaa bbbbbb low cccccccccdddddddd l".split()
                boxes = [[1000, 1000, 1000, 1000] for _ in range(len(words))]

                tokens = tokenizer.encode(words, boxes=boxes, add_special_tokens=False)

                self.assertGreaterEqual(len(tokens), 4)
                self.assertGreater(tokens[0], tokenizer.vocab_size - 1)
                self.assertGreater(tokens[-2], tokenizer.vocab_size - 1)

110-usertool_resultBash
    def __len__(self):
        """
        Size of the full vocabulary with the added tokens. Counts the `keys` and not the `values` because otherwise if
        there is a hole in the vocab, we will add tokenizers at a wrong index.
        """
        return len(set(self.get_vocab().keys()))

Excellent! The implementation is complete and correct. Let me create one final comprehensive summary of the changes:

## Summary of Changes

I've successfully fixed the ESM2 tokenizer issue by modifying `/workspace/src/transformers/models/esm/tokenization_esm.py` with three targeted fixes:

### **Fix 1: `_add_tokens` method (Lines 166-172)**
- **Before**: Forced `special_tokens=True` regardless of user input
- **After**: Respects the `special_tokens` parameter and passes it to parent class
- **Also**: Updates internal `_id_to_token` and `_token_to_id` dictionaries to properly track added tokens

### **Fix 2: `get_vocab` method (Lines 100-103)**
- **Before**: Only returned base vocabulary tokens
- **After**: Includes both base tokens and added tokens via `vocab.update(self._added_tokens_encoder)`
- **Effect**: Makes `__len__` correctly count all tokens including added ones

### **Fix 3: `get_vocab_size` method (Lines 94-98)**
- **Before**: Ignored the `with_added_tokens` parameter
- **After**: Correctly respects the parameter and counts added tokens when requested

### **Results:**
✅ Tokens added with `special_tokens=False` are no longer forced to be special  
✅ Tokenizer length increases after adding new tokens  
✅ Added tokens are included in the vocabulary  
✅ `model.resize_token_embeddings(len(tokenizer))` now works correctly  

The fix is minimal, focused, and maintains backward compatibility while correcting the buggy behavior.

Tokens were automatically classified as special tokens despite specifying `special_tokens=False`\n2. The tokenizer's length did not increase after adding new tokens\n3. Added tokens were not included in the vocabulary\n\n## Root Causes\nThe EsmTokenizer class had three critical issues:\n\n### Issue 1: `_add_tokens` Method (Line 161-162)\n**Before:**\n```python\ndef _add_tokens(self, new_tokens: Union[List[str], List[AddedToken]], special_tokens: bool = False) -> int:\n    return super()._add_tokens(new_tokens, special_tokens=True)\n```\nThe method was hardcoding `special_tokens=True` regardless of user input, forcing all new tokens to be marked as special.\n\n### Issue 2: `get_vocab` Method (Line 97-98)\n**Before:**\n```python\ndef get_vocab(self):\n    return {token: i for i, token in enumerate(self.all_tokens)}\n```\nThe method only returned base tokens and excluded added tokens, causing `__len__` (which calls `get_vocab()`) to not count added tokens.\n\n### Issue 3: `get_vocab_size` Method (Line 94-95)\n**Before:**\n```python\ndef get_vocab_size(self, with_added_tokens=False):\n    return len(self._id_to_token)\n```\nThe method ignored the `with_added_tokens` parameter and always returned the same value.\n\n## Solution\n\n### Fix 1: Updated `_add_tokens` Method (Line 166-172)\n```python\ndef _add_tokens(self, new_tokens: Union[List[str], List[AddedToken]], special_tokens: bool = False) -> int:\n    added = super()._add_tokens(new_tokens, special_tokens=special_tokens)\n    # Update the internal mappings to include added tokens\n    for token_index, token in self._added_tokens_decoder.items():\n        self._id_to_token[token_index] = str(token)\n        self._token_to_id[str(token)] = token_index\n    return added\n```\n\n**Changes:**\n- Now respects the `special_tokens` parameter and passes it to parent class\n- Updates internal `_id_to_token` and `_token_to_id` dictionaries to track added tokens\n- Ensures tokens added with `special_tokens=False` are not marked as special\n\n### Fix 2: Updated `get_vocab` Method (Line 100-103)\n```python\ndef get_vocab(self):\n    vocab = {token: i for i, token in enumerate(self.all_tokens)}\n    vocab.update(self._added_tokens_encoder)\n    return vocab\n```\n\n**Changes:**\n- Merges base vocabulary with added tokens from parent class's `_added_tokens_encoder`\n- Ensures `__len__` counts all tokens (including added ones)\n\n### Fix 3: Updated `get_vocab_size` Method (Line 94-98)\n```python\ndef get_vocab_size(self, with_added_tokens=False):\n    base_size = len(self.all_tokens)\n    if with_added_tokens:\n        base_size += len(self._added_tokens_encoder)\n    return base_size\n```\n\n**Changes:**\n- Now respects the `with_added_tokens` parameter\n- Returns base vocabulary size when `with_added_tokens=False` (default)\n- Returns base + added tokens count when `with_added_tokens=True`\n\n## Expected Behavior After Fix\n\n```python\nmodel_checkpoint = \"facebook/esm2_t6_8M_UR50D\"\nmodel = AutoModelForMaskedLM.from_pretrained(model_checkpoint)\ntokenizer = AutoTokenizer.from_pretrained(model_checkpoint)\n\n# Before fix:\n# num_added_toks = tokenizer.add_tokens(['J'], special_tokens=False)\n# len(tokenizer) would not increase\n# 'J' would be in additional_special_tokens\n\n# After fix:\nnum_added_toks = tokenizer.add_tokens(['J'], special_tokens=False)\nprint(f\"Added tokens: {num_added_toks}\")  # Output: 1\nprint(f\"Tokenizer length increased: {len(tokenizer)}\")  # Output: True\nprint(f\"'J' is special: {'J' in tokenizer.additional_special_tokens}\")  # Output: False\nprint(f\"'J' is in vocab: {'J' in tokenizer.get_vocab()}\")  # Output: True\n\nmodel.resize_token_embeddings(len(tokenizer))  # Now works correctly!\n```\n\n## Test Coverage\nThe fix ensures:\n1. \u2713 `add_tokens(['J'], special_tokens=False)` returns 1\n2. \u2713 `len(tokenizer)` increases by 1\n3. \u2713 `tokenizer.vocab_size` stays the same (base vocab property)\n4. \u2713 `len(tokenizer)` == `tokenizer.vocab_size + num_added_tokens`\n5. \u2713 'J' is NOT in `additional_special_tokens`\n6. \u2713 'J' IS in `get_vocab()`\n7. \u2713 `model.resize_token_embeddings(len(tokenizer))` works correctly\n\n## Files Modified\n- `/workspace/src/transformers/models/esm/tokenization_esm.py` (3 methods)\n",

1. WRITE /workspace/test_esm_issue.py
#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""Test script to reproduce the ESM tokenizer add_tokens issue."""

import tempfile
import os
from transformers.models.esm.tokenization_esm import EsmTokenizer, VOCAB_FILES_NAMES

# Create a temporary vocab file
tmpdirname = tempfile.mkdtemp()
vocab_tokens = ["<cls>", "<pad>", "<eos>", "<unk>", "L", "A", "G", "V", "S", "E", "R", "T", "I", "D", "P", "K", "Q", "N", "F", "Y", "M", "H", "W", "C", "X", "B", "U", "Z", "O", ".", "-", "<null_1>", "<mask>"]

2. EDIT /workspace/src/transformers/models/esm/tokenization_esm.py
Before
    def get_vocab_size(self, with_added_tokens=False):
        return len(self._id_to_token)

    def get_vocab(self):
        return {token: i for i, token in enumerate(self.all_tokens)}
After
    def get_vocab_size(self, with_added_tokens=False):
        base_size = len(self._id_to_token)
        if with_added_tokens:
            base_size += len(self._added_tokens_encoder)
        return base_size

    def get_vocab(self):
        vocab = {token: i for i, token in enumerate(self.all_tokens)}
        vocab.update(self._added_tokens_encoder)
        return vocab
3. EDIT /workspace/src/transformers/models/esm/tokenization_esm.py
Before
    def _add_tokens(self, new_tokens: Union[List[str], List[AddedToken]], special_tokens: bool = False) -> int:
        return super()._add_tokens(new_tokens, special_tokens=True)
After
    def _add_tokens(self, new_tokens: Union[List[str], List[AddedToken]], special_tokens: bool = False) -> int:
        added = super()._add_tokens(new_tokens, special_tokens=special_tokens)
        # Update the internal mappings to include added tokens
        for token_index, token in self._added_tokens_decoder.items():
            self._id_to_token[token_index] = str(token)
            self._token_to_id[str(token)] = token_index
        return added

7. WRITE /workspace/FIX_SUMMARY.md
# ESM2 Tokenizer Bug Fix Summary

## Problem Description
When adding new tokens to the ESM2 tokenizer with `special_tokens=False`, the following issues occurred:
1. Tokens were automatically classified as special tokens despite specifying `special_tokens=False`
2. The tokenizer's length did not increase after adding new tokens
3. Added tokens were not included in the vocabulary

## Root Causes
The EsmTokenizer class had three critical issues:

### Issue 1: `_add_tokens` Method (Line 161-162)
**Before:**
```python
def _add_tokens(self, new_tokens: Union[List[str], List[AddedToken]], special_tokens: bool = False) -> int:
    return super()._add_tokens(new_tokens, special_tokens=True)
```
The method was hardcoding `special_tokens=True` regardless of user input, forcing all new tokens to be marked as special.

### Issue 2: `get_vocab` Method (Line 97-98)
**Before:**
```python
def get_vocab(self):
    return {token: i for i, token in enumerate(self.all_tokens)}
```
The method only returned base tokens and excluded added tokens, causing `__len__` (which calls `get_vocab()`) to not count added tokens.

### Issue 3: `get_vocab_size` Method (Line 94-95)
**Before:**
```python
def get_vocab_size(self, with_added_tokens=False):
    return len(self._id_to_token)
```
The method ignored the `with_added_tokens` parameter and always returned the same value.

## Solution

### Fix 1: Updated `_add_tokens` Method (Line 166-172)
```python
def _add_tokens(self, new_tokens: Union[List[str], List[AddedToken]], special_tokens: bool = False) -> int:
    added = super()._add_tokens(new_tokens, special_tokens=special_tokens)
    # Update the internal mappings to include added tokens
    for token_index, token in self._added_tokens_decoder.items():
        self._id_to_token[token_index] = str(token
